Allah's Transcendence Above the Throne
Quotes affirming Allah's transcendence and knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the Salaf position that Allah is above the Throne, distinct from creation, while His knowledge encompasses all places.

Core Idea
Allah is above, yet His knowledge is everywhere—no contradiction.

The Salaf affirmed Allah's 'above-ness' (al-fawqiyya) literally, without claiming to know the 'how'. At the same time, they upheld His complete knowledge of all things. This lesson extracts the key creedal statements from Malik, Ibn al-Mubarak, Sufyan, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, and shows how to distinguish the Salafi position from the Jahmiyya denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures and their statements
Read each quote: Malik says 'Allah is in the heaven, His knowledge in every place.' Ibn al-Mubarak says 'above the heavens on the Throne, distinct from creation.' Sufyan interprets 'He is with you' as His knowledge. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad affirm His establishedness on the Throne and universal knowledge.
Notice that all agree on Allah's transcendence without negating His immanence through knowledge.
2
Compare with the Jahmiyya position mentioned
Ibn al-Mubarak explicitly rejects the Jahmiyya who say 'He is here' (pointing to earth). The Salaf avoid both anthropomorphism and denial of attributes.
This refutes the false dichotomy that either Allah is everywhere physically or He is nowhere.
3
Extract the principle: transcendence with immanent knowledge
The Salaf do not say Allah's essence is everywhere. They say His knowledge encompasses all. This reconciles the verses of 'above-ness' with 'He is with you.'
This principle is foundational for understanding Allah's relationship to creation.
4
Memorize the key formulation from Malik
Malik's concise statement is a memorization anchor: 'Allah is in the heaven, and His knowledge is in every place.'
It captures the entire lesson in one line.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال مالك: إن الله في السَّماء، وعلمه في كل مكان. وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: نعرف ربنا فوق سبع سمواته على العرش بائنا من خلقه، ولا نقول كما قالت الجهمية: إنه هاهنا، وأشار إلى الأرض. وقال سفيان الثوري: ﴿وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ﴾ قال: علمه. قال الشافعي: إنه على عرشه في سمائه يقربُ من خلقه كيف شاء. قال أحمد: إنه مستو على العرش، عالم بكل مكان. وأنه ينزل كلَّ ليلة إلى السَّماء الدُّنيا كيف شاء، وأنه يأتي يوم القيامة كيف شاء، وأنه يعلو على كرسيه، والإيمان بالعرش والكرسي وما ورد فيهما من الآيات والأخبار، وأن الكَلِمَ الطَّيِّبَ يصعد إليه، وتعرج الملائكة والروح إليه، وأنه خلق آدم بيديه وخلق القلم وجنَّة عَدْنٍ وشجرة طوبى بيديه وكتب التوراة بيديه، وأن كلتا يديه يمين. وقال ابن عمر: خلق الله بيديه أربعة أشياء: آدم، والعرش، والقلم، وجنَّة عدن، وقال لسائر الخلق كُن، فكان. وأنه يتكلم بالوحي كيف يشاء. قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها: لَشَأني في نفسي كان أحقر من أن يتكلم الله فيَّ بوحي يتلى. وأن القرآن كلام الله بجميع جهاته، منزّل غير مخلوق، ولا حرف منه مخلوق، منه بدأ وإليه يعود. قال عبد الله بن المبارك من كفَر بحرفٍ من القرآن فقد كفر، ومن قـال: لا أؤمن بهذه اللام فقد كفر. وأن الكتب المنزّلة على الرُّسل مئة وأربعة كتب كلام الله غير مخلوق. قال أحمد: وما في اللوح المحفوظ، وما في المصاحف وتلاوة الناس، وكيفما يُقرأ، وكيفما يوصف، فهو كلام الله غير مخلوق. قال البخاري وأقول: في المصحف قرآن، وفي صدور الرجال قرآن، فمن قال غير هذا يُستتاب، فإن تاب وإلا فسبيله سبيلُ الكفر.
Malik said: Indeed Allah is in the heaven, and His knowledge is in every place. And Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: We know our Lord above seven heavens on the Throne, distinct from His creation, and we do not say as the Jahmiyya say: He is here, and he pointed to the ground. And Sufyan al-Thawri said: 'And He is with you wherever you are' – he said: His knowledge. Al-Shafi'i said: He is on His Throne in His heaven, He draws near to His creation as He wills. Ahmad said: He is established on the Throne, knowing every place. And that He descends every night to the lowest heaven as He wills, and that He comes on the Day of Judgment as He wills, and that He rises over His Kursi, and belief in the Throne and the Kursi and what has come in verses and reports concerning them, and that good words ascend to Him, and the angels and the Spirit ascend to Him, and that He created Adam with His hands, and created the Pen, and the Garden of Eden, and the Tree of Tuba with His hands, and wrote the Torah with His hands, and that both His hands are right hands. And Ibn Umar said: Allah created with His hands four things: Adam, the Throne, the Pen, and the Garden of Eden, and He said to the rest of creation 'Be', so they were. And that He speaks with revelation as He wills. Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, said: My affair in myself was too insignificant for Allah to speak about me in revelation that is recited. And that the Quran is the speech of Allah in all its aspects, revealed, uncreated, and no letter of it is created, from Him it began and to Him it returns. Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: Whoever disbelieves in a letter of the Quran has disbelieved, and whoever says 'I do not believe in this lam' has disbelieved. And that the books revealed to the messengers, one hundred and four books, are the speech of Allah, uncreated. Ahmad said: And what is in the Preserved Tablet, and what is in the copies (mushafs) and the recitation of people, however it is recited and however it is described, it is the speech of Allah, uncreated. Al-Bukhari said: I say: In the mushaf is the Quran, and in the breasts of men is the Quran. Whoever says otherwise is to be asked to repent; if he repents, otherwise his path is the path of disbelief.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of statements from early Muslim scholars (Salaf) regarding Allah's attributes and the nature of the Quran. It serves as a foundational text for the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah in refuting the Jahmiyya and rationalist logicians who deny or allegorize these attributes. The passage proceeds in order: first, quotes affirming that Allah is above the heavens on the Throne, yet His knowledge encompasses all places (Malik, Ibn al-Mubarak, Sufyan, Shafi'i, Ahmad). Second, it elaborates on Allah's actions: His descent to the lowest heaven, His coming on Judgment Day, His creation of Adam, the Pen, Paradise, and the Torah with His hands, and that both His hands are right hands. The quote from Ibn Umar specifies four things created by Allah's hands. Third, it addresses Allah's speech: that He speaks by revelation as He wills, illustrated by Aisha's statement about the slander incident. Fourth, it emphatically states the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah in every respect—not a single letter created—and that the scriptures (104 books) are likewise uncreated. Ahmad's statement includes the Preserved Tablet, written copies, and oral recitation as uncreated speech. Finally, al-Bukhari asserts that the Quran in the mushaf and in hearts is the Quran, and anyone who denies this must repent or be treated as a disbeliever. The passage guards against two extremes: anthropomorphism (by affirming 'how' is unknown) and negation of attributes (by affirming them as described).

Key Terms
العرش
العلم
مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He said it means Allah's essence is everywhere.
B) He said it means Allah's knowledge is everywhere.
C) He said it refers to the angels.
D) He said it was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf affirm that Allah is above the Throne, distinct from creation, yet His knowledge encompasses all places.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Write a short explanation for someone who asks: 'If Allah is above the heavens, how can He be with us?' Use the Salaf responses from this lesson.
?
Identify the logical error in the Jahmiyya claim 'He is here' based on the Salaf's distinction between Allah's essence and His knowledge.

The Uncreated Quran: Speech of Allah
Emphatic declaration of Quran being uncreated speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Salaf doctrine that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah in all aspects, and explain the ruling on those who claim it is created.

Core Idea
Every letter of the Quran is uncreated; to deny this is apostasy.

The passage emphatically declares that the Quran is Allah's speech, uncreated, from its letters to its recitation. It cites Ahmad, Ibn al-Mubarak, and al-Bukhari, and concludes that any denial necessitates repentance or disbelief. This lesson unpacks those statements and their theological weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim about the Quran
The passage states: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah in all its aspects, revealed, uncreated, and no letter of it is created.' Also, the books revealed to messengers (104 total) are uncreated.
The phrase 'in all its aspects' (bi-jami' jihatihi) is key: it includes the words, letters, and meanings.
2
Examine the scope of 'uncreated' according to Ahmad
Ahmad says: 'What is in the Preserved Tablet, and what is in the copies (mushafs) and the recitation of people... it is the speech of Allah, uncreated.' This includes the written and recited Quran.
This refutes the later Ash'ari distinction between eternal meaning and temporal expression.
3
Understand the consequence of denying this
Ibn al-Mubarak: 'Whoever disbelieves in a letter of the Quran has disbelieved.' Al-Bukhari: 'Whoever says otherwise is to be asked to repent; if not, his path is the path of disbelief.'
This shows the gravity of the issue: it is a matter of iman and kufr.
4
Memorize the formula: 'minhu bada wa ilayhi ya'ud'
The phrase 'from Him it began and to Him it returns' encapsulates the Quran's divine origin and ultimate return.
This is a concise creedal statement often used in debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال مالك: إن الله في السَّماء، وعلمه في كل مكان. وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: نعرف ربنا فوق سبع سمواته على العرش بائنا من خلقه، ولا نقول كما قالت الجهمية: إنه هاهنا، وأشار إلى الأرض. وقال سفيان الثوري: ﴿وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ﴾ قال: علمه. قال الشافعي: إنه على عرشه في سمائه يقربُ من خلقه كيف شاء. قال أحمد: إنه مستو على العرش، عالم بكل مكان. وأنه ينزل كلَّ ليلة إلى السَّماء الدُّنيا كيف شاء، وأنه يأتي يوم القيامة كيف شاء، وأنه يعلو على كرسيه، والإيمان بالعرش والكرسي وما ورد فيهما من الآيات والأخبار، وأن الكَلِمَ الطَّيِّبَ يصعد إليه، وتعرج الملائكة والروح إليه، وأنه خلق آدم بيديه وخلق القلم وجنَّة عَدْنٍ وشجرة طوبى بيديه وكتب التوراة بيديه، وأن كلتا يديه يمين. وقال ابن عمر: خلق الله بيديه أربعة أشياء: آدم، والعرش، والقلم، وجنَّة عدن، وقال لسائر الخلق كُن، فكان. وأنه يتكلم بالوحي كيف يشاء. قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها: لَشَأني في نفسي كان أحقر من أن يتكلم الله فيَّ بوحي يتلى. وأن القرآن كلام الله بجميع جهاته، منزّل غير مخلوق، ولا حرف منه مخلوق، منه بدأ وإليه يعود. قال عبد الله بن المبارك من كفَر بحرفٍ من القرآن فقد كفر، ومن قـال: لا أؤمن بهذه اللام فقد كفر. وأن الكتب المنزّلة على الرُّسل مئة وأربعة كتب كلام الله غير مخلوق. قال أحمد: وما في اللوح المحفوظ، وما في المصاحف وتلاوة الناس، وكيفما يُقرأ، وكيفما يوصف، فهو كلام الله غير مخلوق. قال البخاري وأقول: في المصحف قرآن، وفي صدور الرجال قرآن، فمن قال غير هذا يُستتاب، فإن تاب وإلا فسبيله سبيلُ الكفر.
Malik said: Indeed Allah is in the heaven, and His knowledge is in every place. And Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: We know our Lord above seven heavens on the Throne, distinct from His creation, and we do not say as the Jahmiyya say: He is here, and he pointed to the ground. And Sufyan al-Thawri said: 'And He is with you wherever you are' – he said: His knowledge. Al-Shafi'i said: He is on His Throne in His heaven, He draws near to His creation as He wills. Ahmad said: He is established on the Throne, knowing every place. And that He descends every night to the lowest heaven as He wills, and that He comes on the Day of Judgment as He wills, and that He rises over His Kursi, and belief in the Throne and the Kursi and what has come in verses and reports concerning them, and that good words ascend to Him, and the angels and the Spirit ascend to Him, and that He created Adam with His hands, and created the Pen, and the Garden of Eden, and the Tree of Tuba with His hands, and wrote the Torah with His hands, and that both His hands are right hands. And Ibn Umar said: Allah created with His hands four things: Adam, the Throne, the Pen, and the Garden of Eden, and He said to the rest of creation 'Be', so they were. And that He speaks with revelation as He wills. Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, said: My affair in myself was too insignificant for Allah to speak about me in revelation that is recited. And that the Quran is the speech of Allah in all its aspects, revealed, uncreated, and no letter of it is created, from Him it began and to Him it returns. Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: Whoever disbelieves in a letter of the Quran has disbelieved, and whoever says 'I do not believe in this lam' has disbelieved. And that the books revealed to the messengers, one hundred and four books, are the speech of Allah, uncreated. Ahmad said: And what is in the Preserved Tablet, and what is in the copies (mushafs) and the recitation of people, however it is recited and however it is described, it is the speech of Allah, uncreated. Al-Bukhari said: I say: In the mushaf is the Quran, and in the breasts of men is the Quran. Whoever says otherwise is to be asked to repent; if he repents, otherwise his path is the path of disbelief.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of statements from early Muslim scholars (Salaf) regarding Allah's attributes and the nature of the Quran. It serves as a foundational text for the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah in refuting the Jahmiyya and rationalist logicians who deny or allegorize these attributes. The passage proceeds in order: first, quotes affirming that Allah is above the heavens on the Throne, yet His knowledge encompasses all places (Malik, Ibn al-Mubarak, Sufyan, Shafi'i, Ahmad). Second, it elaborates on Allah's actions: His descent to the lowest heaven, His coming on Judgment Day, His creation of Adam, the Pen, Paradise, and the Torah with His hands, and that both His hands are right hands. The quote from Ibn Umar specifies four things created by Allah's hands. Third, it addresses Allah's speech: that He speaks by revelation as He wills, illustrated by Aisha's statement about the slander incident. Fourth, it emphatically states the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah in every respect—not a single letter created—and that the scriptures (104 books) are likewise uncreated. Ahmad's statement includes the Preserved Tablet, written copies, and oral recitation as uncreated speech. Finally, al-Bukhari asserts that the Quran in the mushaf and in hearts is the Quran, and anyone who denies this must repent or be treated as a disbeliever. The passage guards against two extremes: anthropomorphism (by affirming 'how' is unknown) and negation of attributes (by affirming them as described).

Key Terms
الكلام
القرآن
مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of a person who says 'I do not believe in this letter of the Quran' according to Ibn al-Mubarak?
A) He is a sinner but remains a Muslim.
B) He is excused because letters are human-made.
C) He has disbelieved.
D) He should be taught but not punished.

Key Takeaway
The Quran in every aspect—letter, word, written copy, recitation—is the uncreated speech of Allah, and denying its uncreatedness is apostasy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Explain to a fellow Muslim why, according to the Salaf, it is not permissible to say 'the Quran is created' even if referring to the ink and paper.
?
Find a contemporary claim that the Quran is 'created in time' (like some modernists) and refute it using the statements of Ahmad and al-Bukhari from this lesson.

Affirming Allah's Acts and Attributes Without Ta'wil
Affirmation of Allah's attributes and acts without ta'wil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the attributes and acts of Allah affirmed by the Salaf in this passage (hand, descent, coming, creation) and explain how they affirm them without tashbih.

Core Idea
The Salaf affirm divine attributes as described, without specifying 'how'.

The passage includes several statements about Allah's actions: He descends, He comes, He created Adam with His hands, and both hands are right hands. These are affirmations of attributes that later sectarians allegorized or denied. This lesson shows the Salaf method: acceptance without interpretation beyond the apparent, while negating resemblance to creation.

Guided Path
1
List the attributes and acts mentioned
From Ahmad: descent (yanzilu), coming (ya'ti), rising over the Kursi, creation with hands (bi-yadayhi), writing the Torah with hands. Ibn Umar: four things created with hands (Adam, Throne, Pen, Garden). Aisha: Allah speaking revelation about her.
These are all attributes of action (sifat fi'liyya) or attributes of essence (sifat dhatiyya) like 'hand'.
2
Identify the Salaf methodology (bila kayf)
Ahmad says 'how He wills' for descent and coming. This indicates affirmation without modality. The passage does not interpret these actions metaphorically.
The principle is: affirm what Allah affirmed for Himself, without asking 'how' (takyif) or making comparisons (tashbih).
3
Distinguish from tashbih (anthropomorphism)
The Salaf did not say Allah's hand is like a human hand. They affirmed 'hand' as an attribute befitting Allah. Ibn Umar's statement that both hands are right hands is to negate deficiency, not to imply physicality.
The common misunderstanding (see below) warns against this.
4
Connect to the broader creed: iman bi al-ghayb
Believing in these reports is part of iman. Aisha's statement about the slander shows that even a great event like revelation about her is part of Allah's speech, which we accept without questioning.
This cultivates a mindset of submission to divine revelation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Salaf's Methodology for Divine Attributes
Author cites Salaf on accepting hadith attributes without tahrif or ta'wil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six principles of the Salaf for handling divine attributes and distinguish them from ta'wil and ta'til.

Core Idea
The Salaf accept divine attributes as revealed, without interpretation or negation, entrusting their reality to Allah.

The passage presents the epistemological foundation for dealing with the attributes of Allah mentioned in the Qur'an and hadith. The Salaf—the earliest and most authoritative generations—established a clear method: accept the texts, refrain from distorting, qualifying, negating, or interpreting them, and do not subject them to human reason or liken them to creation. This lesson unpacks that methodology and shows why it remains the benchmark for orthodox Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six negative principles
The passage lists six things the Salaf do NOT do: they do not distort (tahrif), do not qualify modality (takyif), do not negate (ta'til), do not interpret figuratively (ta'wil), do not burden intellects, do not liken to creation. Highlight each in the Arabic.
These six encapsulate the via media between anthropomorphism and negation.
2
Identify the positive actions
What do they do? They accept (naqbal), believe (nu'min), entrust knowledge to Allah (nakilu 'ilmaha ila 'alimiha), and follow the Salaf's example.
The positive action is belief and trust in Allah's knowledge.
3
Analyze the citations of early scholars
The passage quotes Ishaq ibn Rahwayh, Malik, al-Awza'i, Sufyan, al-Layth, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Notice the consistency: all say to narrate and believe without interpretation.
This shows the consensus among early scholars across regions and madhhabs.
4
Contrast with the theologians (mutakallimun)
The author ends by criticizing theologians who misrepresent the Hanbalis. Identify the key difference: the Salaf stop where the text stops; the theologians apply speculative interpretation.
This contrast highlights the epistemological divide: revelation-based vs reason-based theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَن بَعُدَ كما يسمعُه مَن قَرُبَ: أنا الملك، أنا الدَّيَّان. إلى غيرها من الأحاديث، هالتنا أو لم تهلنا، بَلَغَتُنا أو لم تَبْلُغُنا، اعتقادنا فيها وفي الآي الواردة في الصفات أنا نقبلها، ولا نحرفها، ولا نكيفها، ولا نعطّلها، ولا نتأوَّلها، وعلى العقول لا نَحْمِلها، وبصفات الخلق لا نشبهها، ولا نُعْمِلُ رأينا وفكرنا فيها، ولا نزيد عليها ولا تُنْقِصُ منها، بل نؤمن بها ونَكِلُ علمها إلى عالمها، كما فعل ذلك السَّلف الصالح، وهم القدوة لنا في كل علم. رُوِّينا عن إسحاق أنه قال: لا نزيل صفةً مما وصف الله به نفسه أو وصف الرسول عن جهته، لا بكلام ولا بإرادة، إنما يلزم المسلم الأداء، ويوقن بقلبه أن ما وصف الله به نفسه في القرآن إنما هي صفاته، ولا يَعْقِلُ نبي مرسل ولا ملك مقرب تلك الصفات إلا بالأسماء التي عرفهم الرب عز وجل، فأما أن يدرك أحد من بني آدم معنى تلك الصفات فلا يدركه أحد. وكما رُوِّينا عن مالك، والأوزاعي، وسفيان، والليث، وأحمد بن حنبل، أنهم قالوا في الأحاديث في الرؤية والنزول: أمروها كما جاءت. وكما روي عن محمد بن الحسن - صاحب أبي حنيفة - أنه قال في الأحاديث التي جاءت إن الله يَهْبِطُ إلى السماء الدنيا ونحـو هـذا مــن الأحاديث: إن هذه الأحاديث قد رواها الثقات، فنحن نرويها ونؤمن بها، ولا نفسرها. أنتهى كلام الكَرَجي رحمه الله تعالى. والعجب أن هؤلاء المتكلمين إذا أحتج عليهم بما في الآيات والأحاديث من الصفات قالوا: قالت الحنابلة: إن الله كذا وكذا، بما فيه تشنيع وترويج لباطلهم، والحنابلة أقتفوا أثر السلف، وساروا بسيرهم، ووقفوا بوقوفهم بخلاف غيرهم، والله الموفق.
Who is far away hears as who is near: 'I am the King, I am the Judge.' And other hadiths, whether they frighten us or not, whether they have reached us or not, our belief in them and in the verses about the attributes is that we accept them, do not distort them, do not qualify them, do not negate them, do not interpret them, do not burden them upon intellects, do not liken them to attributes of creation, do not employ our opinion and thought in them, do not add to them nor subtract from them. Rather, we believe in them and entrust their knowledge to the One who knows them, just as the righteous Salaf did—they are our exemplars in all knowledge. We have narrated from Ishaq that he said: 'We do not remove any attribute with which Allah described Himself or the Messenger described Him from its status, neither by speech nor by will. The Muslim is only obliged to convey, and to be certain in his heart that what Allah described Himself with in the Qur'an are His attributes. No sent prophet nor close angel comprehends those attributes except by the names by which the Lord, Mighty and Majestic, made them known. As for any son of Adam perceiving the meaning of those attributes, no one can perceive it.' And as we narrated from Malik, al-Awza'i, Sufyan, al-Layth, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal—they said regarding the hadiths about seeing and descending: 'Let them pass as they came.' And as narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the companion of Abu Hanifa, that he said regarding the hadiths that came that Allah descends to the lowest heaven and similar hadiths: 'These hadiths have been narrated by trustworthy people, so we narrate them, believe in them, and do not interpret them.' End of the speech of al-Karaji, may Allah have mercy on him. And it is amazing that these theologians, when argued against by what is in the verses and hadiths of attributes, say: 'The Hanbalis say such and such about Allah,' thereby discrediting and promoting their falsehood, while the Hanbalis have followed the path of the Salaf, walked in their way, and stopped where they stopped, unlike others. Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents the epistemological methodology of the Salaf regarding the divine attributes mentioned in the Qur'an and hadith. The author begins by affirming that the Salaf accept these attributes without alteration (tahrif), without specifying modality (takyif), without negation (ta'til), and without figurative interpretation (ta'wil). They do not subject these attributes to human reason or liken them to creation. Instead, they believe them and entrust their true knowledge to Allah. The author then cites specific statements from early scholars: Ishaq ibn Rahwayh emphasizes that no one, not even prophets or angels, comprehends the reality of these attributes except as Allah has named them. Malik, al-Awza'i, Sufyan al-Thawri, al-Layth ibn Sa'd, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal all instructed to let the hadiths about seeing Allah and His descent pass as they came, without interpretation. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, a Hanafi scholar, similarly narrates such hadiths and believes them without interpretation. The author concludes by criticizing the theologians (mutakallimun) who misrepresent the Hanbalis, while affirming that the Hanbalis follow the Salaf. The overall lesson is that proper Islamic epistemology includes accepting revelation literally in matters of divine attributes, avoiding both anthropomorphism and negation.

Key Terms
السلف
الصفات
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Malik and Ahmad ibn Hanbal say about hadiths concerning Allah's descent and vision?
A) Interpret them metaphorically to be safe.
B) Reject them as weak narrations.
C) Let them pass as they came.
D) Qualify them with 'without how' but explain their meaning.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's methodology is to affirm divine attributes as revealed, without distortion, modality, negation, or interpretation, entrusting their reality to Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In one sentence, explain why the Salaf did not interpret 'Yad Allah' (the Hand of Allah) as 'power' or 'blessing', as some theologians do.
?
Read the hadith: 'Our Lord descends to the lowest heaven every night.' Identify which of the six negative principles would be violated if you said: 'Descending here means His mercy descends, not His entity.'

Critique of Opponents' Lack of Evidence in Theological Debate
Author critiques opponents for lacking evidence and relying on insults and taqlid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flaws in a theological opponent's methodology according to Ibn Taymiyya's critique, specifically the reliance on taqlid and insults instead of evidence.

Core Idea
Evidence is the only valid currency in theological debate; insults and taqlid are worthless.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya (or a follower) thoroughly critiques the methodology of certain mutakallimun who, when confronted with scriptural evidence regarding Allah's attributes, resort to defaming the Hanabila and relying on taqlid instead of providing substantive proof. The author distinguishes this as a type of response that contains no proof or evidence, merely insults and intimidation. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recognize these flaws and understand the author's demand for genuine evidence in theological discourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of the critique
Find the group being criticized and their flawed methodology. The author criticizes mutakallimun who respond to scriptural evidence by defaming the Hanabila and relying on taqlid.
The target is not the Hanabila but the mutakallimun who attack them without evidence.
2
Locate the author's grounds for critique
What does the author use as basis for his critique? He cites Quranic verses commanding wisdom and good argument, and argues that proper debate requires clear evidence.
The author's grounds are epistemological and revelation-based.
3
Extract the author's alternative approach
What should the opponents have done instead? The author implies that proper debate requires presenting clear evidence (ḥujja sam'iyya or 'aqliyya) as commanded in the Quran.
The alternative is to provide evidence rather than defamation or taqlid.
4
Evaluate the internal validity of the critique
Does the author's own argument meet the standard he sets? The critique itself uses Quranic authority and logical reasoning, thus it is valid.
The author practices what he preaches, providing evidence for his claims.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعجب أن هؤلاء المتكلمين إذا أحتج عليهم بما في الآيات والأحاديث من الصفات قالوا: قالت الحنابلة: إن الله كذا وكذا، بما فيه تشنيع وترويج لباطلهم، والحنابلة أقتفوا أثر السلف، وساروا بسيرهم، ووقفوا بوقوفهم بخلاف غيرهم، والله الموفق.
النوع الثاني: أن هذا الكلام ليس فيه من الحجة والدليل ما يستحق أن يخاطب به أهل العلم، فإن الرد بمجرد الشتم والتهويل لا يعجز عنه أحد، والإنسان لو أنه يناظر المشركين وأهل الكتاب لكان عليه أن يذكر من الحجة ما يبين به الحق الذي معه والباطل الذي معهم، فقد قال الله عز وجل لنبيه: ﴿ادعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَدِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ﴾ [النحل: 125]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُجَادِلُوا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ إِلَّا بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ﴾ [العنكبوت: 46].
فلو كان خصم من يتكلم بهذا الكلام - سواء كان المتكلم به أبو الفرج أو غيره - من أشهر الطوائف بالبدع، كالرافضة = لكان ينبغي أن يذكر الحجة ويعدل عما لا فائدة فيه إذا كان في مقام الرد عليهم، دع والمنازعون له كما أدعاه هم عند جميع الناس أعلم منه بالأصول والفروع.
وهو في كلامه ورده لم يأت بحجة أصلا، لا حجة سمعية ولا عقلية، وإنما اعتمد تقليد طائفة من أهل الكلام قد خالفها أكثر منها من أهل الكلام فقلدهم فيما زعموا أنه حجة عقلية، كما فعل هذا المعترض. ومن يرد على الناس بالمعقول إن لم يبين حجة عقلية وإلا كان قد أحال الناس على المجهولات، كمعصوم الرافضة وغوث بعض الصوفية.
فأما قوله: «إن مثل هؤلاء لا يحدثون»، فيقال له: قد بعث الله الرسل إلى جميع الخلق ليدعوهم إلى الله، فمن الذي أسقط الله مخاطبته من الناس؟ دع من تعرف أنت وغيرك من فضلهم ما ليس هذا موضعه، ولو أراد سفيه أن يرد على الراد بمثل رده لم يعجز عن ذلك.
وكذلك قوله: «إنهم يكابرون العقول»، فنقول: المكابرة للعقول إما أن...
And it is astonishing that these mutakallimun, when they are argued against by what is in the verses and hadiths of the attributes, they say: 'The Hanabila said: Allah is such and such,' including defamation and promotion of their falsehood. And the Hanabila followed the path of the Salaf, and walked in their way, and stopped at their stopings, unlike others. And Allah is the Granter of success. 
The second type: that this speech contains no proof or evidence worthy of addressing the people of knowledge. For responding with mere insult and intimidation is something anyone can do. If a man were to debate the polytheists and the People of the Book, he would have to mention the evidence that clarifies the truth he holds and the falsehood they hold. Allah Almighty said to His Prophet: 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good instruction, and argue with them in a way that is best' [Quran 16:125], and He said: 'And do not argue with the People of the Book except in a way that is best' [Quran 29:46]. 
If the opponent of the one who speaks this speech—whether the speaker is Abu al-Faraj or someone else—is from the most notorious sects of innovation, like the Rafidah, then he should mention the evidence and turn away from what is useless when he is in the position of refuting them. Moreover, his opponents (al-munāziʿūn) as he claims are, in the eyes of all people, more knowledgeable than him in the principles and branches. 
In his speech and his refutation, he brought no evidence at all, neither transmitted evidence nor rational evidence. He merely relied on taqlid of a group of the mutakallimun, which a greater number of mutakallimun have opposed. He blindly followed them in what they claimed was a rational proof, as this objector did. Whoever refutes people with intellectual reasoning, if he does not present a rational proof, then he has referred people to unknowns, like the infallible imam of the Rafidah and the Ghawth of some Sufis. 
As for his statement: 'Such people are not to be addressed,' it is said to him: Allah sent messengers to all creation to call them to Allah. So who has exempted anyone from being addressed by Allah? Leave aside those whose virtue you and others know—this is not the place. If a fool wanted to refute the refuter with a similar refutation, he would not be unable. 
And likewise his statement: 'They contradict the intellects,' we say: Contradicting the intellects either...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the methodology of certain mutakallimun (theologians) who, when confronted with scriptural evidence regarding Allah's attributes, resort to defaming the Hanabila (the followers of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal) instead of providing substantive proof. The author, likely Ibn Taymiyya or a follower, defends the Hanbali approach as adhering to the Salaf. He then categorizes this as the 'second type' of flawed response: speech devoid of proof or evidence, relying only on insults and intimidation. He argues that even when debating polytheists or People of the Book, one must present clear evidence (ḥujja) as commanded in the Quran. The opponent—whether Abu al-Faraj ibn al-Jawzi or another—fails to bring any evidence, be it transmitted (samʿiyya) or rational (ʿaqliyya), instead blindly following (taqlīd) a faction of mutakallimun that is opposed by the majority. The author likens this to appealing to unknown authorities like the Rafidah's infallible imam or the Sufi concept of al-Ghawth. He further refutes the claim that such people should not be addressed, citing that Allah addresses all creation through prophets. Finally, he counters the accusation of 'contradicting intellects' (mukābara) by suggesting that such a claim requires clarification. All examples are rooted in Islamic theological debates.

Key Terms
الحنابلة (al-Ḥanābila): Followers of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, adhering to the Salaf in matters of divine attributes, rejecting ta'wil. [Note: No significant shift; term stable in referring to the Hanbali school.]
الرافضة (al-Rāfiḍa): A derogatory term for Shia who reject (rafḍ) the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Umar; here used as example of an innovated sect. [Note: Term used polemically; in later usage sometimes softened to 'al-Shi'a'.]
الغوث (al-Ghawth): In Sufi terminology, a supreme saint considered the 'succor' of the universe, upon whom cosmic order depends. [Note: Concept of Ghawth becomes more codified in later Sufi hierarchy (Ibn Arabi, etc.).]
تقليد (taqlīd): Blind following of authority without evidence; here pejorative, as the opponent follows a group's claim of rational proof without verification. [Note: In usul al-fiqh, taqlid has a technical meaning; here used broadly as uncritical acceptance.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary flaw in the objector's refutation?
A) He used too many Quranic verses.
B) He relied on taqlid of a minority group and brought no evidence.
C) He was too harsh on the Hanabila.
D) He failed to address the Rafidah.

Key Takeaway
A valid refutation in theological debate must present clear evidence, whether transmitted or rational, and cannot rely on taqlid or insults.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
2. Find a passage from a classical kalam text where a theologian responds to scriptural evidence. Determine whether their response meets the standard of evidence described in this lesson.

The Mutual Entailment of the Three Principles of Faith
Author establishes the mutual entailment of tawheed, risala, and the last day through inductive Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the logical concept of mutual entailment (تلازم) as applied to the three core Islamic beliefs and identify scriptural evidence for their inseparability.

Core Idea
The three principles—tawheed, risala, and the Last Day—are logically inseparable; belief in one entails belief in the others.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates through Quranic evidence that the three fundamental principles of Islam are not independent but mutually entailing. Understanding this interdependence is crucial for a correct Islamic epistemology: rejecting one principle necessarily undermines the others. This lesson will guide you through the logical structure of this scriptural argument and its implications for faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three principles
Locate where the author explicitly names the three principles at the end of the passage: توحيد الله، والإيمان برسله، وباليوم الآخر. Note that these are the core beliefs under discussion.
The third principle is sometimes expressed as 'belief in the Last Day'.
2
Extract the Quranic evidence pattern
Review each Quranic verse cited. Observe how each verse either mentions both the message (risala) and the Last Day together, or implies that coming of messengers leads to accountability on the Last Day. For example, in az-Zumar 71, the disbelievers are driven to Hell and it is mentioned that the message came to them and they were warned of the Last Day.
The verses serve as inductive evidence for the interconnection.
3
Understand the logical term 'mutalāzima'
The author uses the term 'متلازمة' (mutually entailing) to describe the relationship. This is a logical concept from the Islamic tradition meaning that each proposition implies the other. Identify where this term appears and see how the author applies it to the three principles.
In logic, 'luzum' refers to implication; 'mutalāzima' is reciprocal implication.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the unity of prophets
The author extends the argument: belief in one messenger implies belief in all messengers, citing an-Nisa 150-151. Understand that this is another layer of mutual entailment within the principle of risala itself.
This reinforces the idea that the principles are tightly integrated.
5
Formulate the logical conclusion
Combine the evidence: the Quran consistently pairs the messenger and the Last Day, and the author states they are mutually entailing. Therefore, a person who accepts tawheed and prophethood must also accept the Last Day, and vice versa. This is not just a theological claim but an epistemological one: these truths stand or fall together.
This conclusion is essential for debates against those who selectively accept parts of the faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال تعالى: ﴿وَسِيقَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا إِلَى جَهَنَّمَ زُمَرًا حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءُوهَا فُتِحَتْ أَبْوَابُهَا ﴾ الآية [الزمر: ۷۱]، فأخبر عن أهل النار أنهم قد جاءتهم الرسالة، وأُنذِرُوا باليوم الآخر.
وقال تعالى: ﴿وَيَوْمَ يَحْشُرُهُمْ جَمِيعًا يَنمَعْشَرَ الْجِنِّ قَدِ اسْتَكْثَرْتُم مِّنَ الإنس إلى قوله: ﴿ وَشَهِدُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا كَفِرِينَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ۱۲۸ - ۱۳۰]، فأخبر عن جميع الجن والإنس أن الرُّسل بلغتهم رسالة الله وهي آياته، وأنهم أنذروهم اليوم الآخر.
-
وكذلك قال: ﴿قُلْ هَلْ تُليتكُم بِالْأَخْسَرِينَ أَعْمَلًا ) الَّذِينَ ضَلَّ سَعْيُهُمْ فِي الْحَيَوَةِ الدُّنْيَا وَهُمْ يَحْسَبُونَ أَنهُمْ يُحْسِنُونَ صُنعا ) أَوَلَيْكَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا بِنَايَتِ رَبِّهِمْ وَلِقَابِهِ الآية ﴾ [الكهف: ١٠٣ - ١٠٥]، فأخبر أنهم كفروا بآياته وهي رسالته، وبلقائه وهو اليوم الآخر.
وقد أخبر أيضًا في غير موضع بأن الرسالة عمت بني آدم، وأن الرُّسل جاؤوا مبشرين ومنذرين، كما قال تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَكَ بِالْحَقِّ بَشِيرًا وَنَذِيرًا وإن مِنْ أُمَّةٍ إِلَّا خَلَا فِيهَا نَذِيرٌ ﴾ [فاطر: ٢٤]، وقال تعالى: (إِنَّا أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ كَمَا أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى نُوج وَالنَّبِيِّينَ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ ) إلى قوله: ﴿وَكَانَ اللَّهُ عَزِيزًا حَكِيمًا ﴾ [النساء: ١٦٣ - ١٦٥]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا نُرْمِيلُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ إِلَّا مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ فَمَنْ ءَامَنَ وَأَصْلَحَ فَلَا خَوْفٌ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا هُمْ يَحْزَنُونَ )) وَالَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا بِنَايَتِنَا يَمَسُّهُمُ الْعَذَابُ بِمَا كَانُوا يَفْسُقُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ٤٨ ، ٤٩]، فأخبر أن من آمن بالرُّسل وأصلَحَ من الأولين والآخرين فلا خوف عليهم ولا هم يحزنون.
وقال تعالى: ﴿قُلْنَا اهْبِطُوا مِنْهَا جَمِيعًا فَإِمَّا يَأْتِيَنَّكُم مِّنِي هُدًى فَمَن تَبِعَ هُدَايَ فَلَا خَوْفٌ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا هُمْ يَحْزَنُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٣٨]، ومثل قوله: ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ امَنُوا وَالَّذِينَ هَادُوا ) إلى قوله: ﴿فَلَهُمْ أَجْرُهُمْ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ ﴾ الآية [البقرة: ٦٢]، فذكر أن المؤمنين بالله وباليوم الآخر من هؤلاء هم أهل النجاة والسعادة، وذكر في تلك الآية الإيمان بالرُّسل، وفي هذه الآية الإيمان باليوم الآخر؛ لأنهما متلازمان.
وكذلك الإيمانُ بالرُّسل كلّهم متلازم، فمن آمن بواحد منهم فقد آمن بهم كلهم، ومن كفر بواحدٍ منهم فقد كفر بهم كلهم، كما قال تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَكْفُرُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَرُسُلِهِ ) إلى قوله: ﴿ أَوَلَيْكَ هُمُ الْكَفِرُونَ حَقًّا الآية والتي بعدها [النساء: ١٥٠، ١٥١]، فأخبر أن المؤمنين بجميع الرسل هم أهل السعادة، و أن المفرقين بينهم بالإيمان ببعضهم دون بعضي هم الكافرون حقا.
وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَكُلَّ إِنسَنِ أَلْزَمْنَهُ طَبَرَهُ فِي عُنُقِهِ، وَتُخْرِجُ لَهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيِّمَةِ كتبا يَلْقَهُ مَنشُورًا ) أقرأْ كِتَبَكَ كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ حَسِيبًا مَّنِ اهْتَدَى فَإِنَّمَا يَهْتَدِى لِنَفْسِهِ وَمَن ضَلَّ فَإِنَّمَا يَضِلُّ عَلَيْهَا وَلَا نَزِرُ وَازِرَةٌ وِزْرَ أُخْرَى وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولًا ﴾ [الإسراء: ١٣ - ١٥].
فهذه الأصول الثلاثة توحيد الله، والإيمان برسله، وباليوم الآخر، هي أمور متلازمة .
He said, exalted: 'And those who disbelieved will be driven to Hell in groups until, when they arrive at it, its gates are opened...' [az-Zumar: 71], so He informed about the people of the Fire that the message had come to them, and they were warned of the Last Day. And He said, exalted: 'And on the Day when He will gather them all together, O company of jinn, you have [misled] many of mankind...' [al-An'am: 128-130], so He informed about all jinn and humans that the messengers conveyed to them the message of Allah, which is His verses, and that they warned them of the Last Day. Similarly He said: 'Say: Shall I inform you of the greatest losers in deeds? Those whose effort is lost in worldly life while they think they are doing well...' [al-Kahf: 103-105], so He informed that they disbelieved in His verses, which are His message, and in His meeting, which is the Last Day. And He also informed in another place that the message encompassed all the children of Adam, and that the messengers came as bearers of good tidings and warners, as He said: 'Indeed, We have sent you with the truth as a bearer of good tidings and a warner, and there was no nation but that a warner had passed within it' [Fatir: 24], and He said: 'Indeed, We have revealed to you as We revealed to Noah and the prophets after him...' [an-Nisa: 163-165], and He said: 'And We send the messengers only as bearers of good tidings and warners. So whoever believes and reforms, there will be no fear concerning them, nor will they grieve' [al-An'am: 48-49], so He informed that whoever believed in the messengers and reformed, from the first and the last, there is no fear on them nor shall they grieve. And He said: 'We said: Go down from it, all of you. And when guidance comes to you from Me, whoever follows My guidance, there will be no fear concerning them, nor will they grieve' [al-Baqarah: 38], and similar to His saying: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews...' to His saying: '...they will have their reward with their Lord' [al-Baqarah: 62]. He mentioned that the believers in Allah and the Last Day among these are the people of salvation and happiness; and He mentioned in that verse belief in the messengers, and in this verse belief in the Last Day, because they are mutually entailing. Likewise, belief in all the messengers is mutually entailing: whoever believes in one of them has believed in all of them, and whoever disbelieves in one of them has disbelieved in all of them, as He said: 'Indeed, those who disbelieve in Allah and His messengers...' to His saying: '...they are the true disbelievers' and the following [an-Nisa: 150-151]. So He informed that the believers in all the messengers are the people of happiness, and that those who differentiate between them by believing in some and not others are the true disbelievers. And He said: 'And every person We have imposed his fate upon his neck, and We will bring forth for him on the Day of Resurrection a record which he will encounter spread open. Read your book. Sufficient is yourself against you this day as an accountant. Whoever is guided is only guided for [the benefit of] himself. And whoever goes astray only goes astray to its detriment. And no bearer of burdens will bear the burden of another. And We were not to punish [anyone] until We sent a messenger' [al-Isra: 13-15]. So these three principles – tawheed of Allah, belief in His messengers, and the Last Day – are mutually entailing matters.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument from revelation, establishing the interdependence of the three core principles of Islamic faith: tawheed (oneness of Allah, prophethood, and the Last Day. The author (Ibn Taymiyya) cites numerous Quranic verses to demonstrate that these principles are not isolated but mutually entailing (متلازمة). The structure is inductive: multiple scriptural proofs are adduced, each showing that the coming of messengers and the warning of the Last Day are conjoined. For instance, in Surah az-Zumar, the gates of Hell open upon arrival, and the disbelievers had already received the message and warning. Similarly, in Surah al-An'am, the gathered jinn and humans are told that messengers conveyed Allah's verses and warned of the Last Day. The author then notes that the phrase 'believers in Allah and the Last Day' in one verse and 'believers in the messengers' in another indicates mutual entailment: belief in one implies belief in the other. He extends this to the unity of all messengers: belief in one is belief in all, and differentiation is disbelief. The passage culminates in Surah al-Isra, which asserts that punishment only occurs after sending a messenger, underscoring the necessity of prophethood for accountability. The conclusion states that these three principles – tawheed, risala, and the Last Day – are mutually entailing. This is a foundational epistemological claim: reason alone cannot fully establish these, but revelation binds them together.

Key Terms
الرسالة
اليوم الآخر
متلازمة
توحيد الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between belief in the messengers and belief in the Last Day?
A) They are independent; one can believe in the messengers without believing in the Last Day.
B) They are mutually entailing; belief in one implies belief in the other.
C) Belief in the messengers is more important than belief in the Last Day.
D) The Last Day is only for those who reject the messengers.

Key Takeaway
The three principles of tawheed, prophethood, and the Last Day are inseparable in the Quran; accepting one requires accepting all, and rejecting one invalidates faith in the others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a Quranic verse that mentions only two of the three principles. Write a brief paragraph explaining how the third is implied by the principle of mutual entailment argued in this passage.
?
Construct an analogy: using the same logic of mutual entailment, explain why belief in all prophets is necessary. Provide a verse or hadith that supports this.

Knowledge Without Obedience to Messengers is Futile
Author cites Quranic verses and a hadith against knowledge without obedience

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic verses and a hadith to argue that intellectual knowledge alone is insufficient for guidance without following the messengers.

Core Idea
Knowledge without obedience to the messengers leads to ruin.

Before critiquing the logicians, Ibn Taymiyya establishes a foundational principle: knowledge and intellectual faculties are of no benefit if they are not guided by revelation and submission to the messengers. In this passage, he draws on Quranic verses and a prophetic hadith to show that even those who possess great knowledge, wealth, and power are doomed if they oppose the prophets. This lesson unpacks how these scriptural proofs serve as the basis for his attack on the sufficiency of Greek logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Read the first sentence: 'He mentioned... what they were given of powers of perceptions and movements that did not benefit them when they opposed the messengers.' This is the thesis: intellectual faculties (perception, movement) are useless without following the messengers.
This principle is repeated across the verses.
2
Analyze the Quranic verses about enemies of messengers
The author cites verses from Surah al-Ahzab (66-68) and Surah Ghafir (47-48) about the punishment of those who opposed the messengers. Note that these people had power (dominion) and knowledge but used them to reject the truth.
The key is that they possessed 'al-mulk' (dominion) and 'al-ilm' (knowledge) yet were punished.
3
Analyze the verses about hypocrites among the followers
Then he cites verses about those who claim to follow the messengers but are hypocrites: scholars who devour wealth, monks who turn people away, and those who prefer disbelievers. This shows that even among those who recite the Quran and claim piety, hypocrisy can exist.
The term 'nifaq' (hypocrisy) is central.
4
Interpret the hadith of the Quran reciter
The hadith compares four types of people: believers who recite, believers who don't, hypocrites who recite, and hypocrites who don't. The hypocrite who recites has a good smell (outward piety) but bitter taste (inner corruption). This reinforces that recitation (knowledge) alone does not guarantee sincerity.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Connect to the critique of logicians
Ibn Taymiyya is about to argue that the logicians' reliance on definitions and syllogisms without prophetic guidance is like the knowledge of those who opposed the messengers or the hypocrisy of those who recite without faith. Understanding this passage prepares us for that critique.
This lesson is a prelude; the actual logical critique follows later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال سبحانه عن أتباع هؤلاء الأئمة من أهل المُلك والعلم المخالفين للرسل : ( يَوْمَ تُقَلَّبُ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ ) إلى قوله : ( وَالْعَنْهُمْ لَعْنا كبيرا ) [الأحزاب: ٦٦ - ٦٨]، وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذْ يَتَحَاجُّونَ فِي النَّارِ ) إلى :قوله وقَدْ حَكَم بين العِبادِ ) [غافر: ٤٨٠٤٧]. ومثل هذا في القرآن كثير ، يذكر فيه من أقوال أعداء الرسل وأفعالهم وما أوتوه من قوى الإدراكات والحركات التي لم تنفعهم لما خالفوا الرسل. وقد ذكر سبحانه ما في المنتسبين إلى أتباع الرُّسل من العلماء والعُبَّاد والملوك من النفاق والضلال في مثل قوله: ﴿يَتأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِنَّ كَثِيرًا مِنَ الْأَحْبَارِ وَالرُّهْبَانِ لَيَأْكُلُونَ أَمْوَالَ النَّاسِ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَيَصُدُّونَ عَن سَبِيلِ الله وَالَّذِينَ يَكْذِرُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَةَ وَلَا يُنفِقُونَهَا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَبَشِّرْهُم بِعَذَابٍ أَلِيمٍ ) [التوبة: ٣٤]، ﴿وَيَصُدُّونَ عَن سَبِيلِ الله الله يستعمل لازما ، يقال : صَدَّ صدودًا، أي أعرض، كما قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذَا قِيلَ هُمْ تَعَالَوْا إِلَى مَا أَنزَلَ اللهُ وَإِلَى الرَّسُولِ رَأَيْتَ الْمُنَافِقِينَ يَصُدُّونَ عَنكَ صُدُودًا ﴾ [النساء: ٦١] ، ويقال : صدَّ غيرَه يَصُدُّهُ، والوصفان يجتمعان فيهم. ومثل قوله: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَ إِلَى الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا نَصِيبًا مِّنَ الْكِتَبِ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِالْجِبْتِ وَالطَّاغُوتِ وَيَقُولُونَ لِلَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا هَؤُلَاءِ أَهْدَى مِنَ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا سَبِيلًا ) [النساء: ٥١]. وفي الصحيحين (۱) عن أبي موسى، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مثلُ المؤمن الذي يقرأ القرآن مثلُ الأترجة طعمها طيب وريحها طيب، ومثل المؤمن الذي لا يقرأ القرآن مثل التمرة طعمُها طيِّبٌ ولا ريحَ لها، ومثلُ المنافق الذي يقرأ القرآن مثلُ الرَّيحانة ريحها طيب وطعمها مر ، ومثل المنافق الذي لا يقرأ القرآن مثلُ الحنظلة طعمها مر ولا ريحَ لها، فبين أن في الذين يقرؤون القرآن مؤمنين ومنافقين
And He, glorified, said about the followers of these leaders from among the people of dominion and knowledge who opposed the messengers: (On the Day when their faces are turned over in the Fire) up to His saying: (and curse them with a great curse) [Al-Ahzab 66-68]. And He, exalted, said: (And when they argue in the Fire) up to His saying: (and judgment has been passed between the servants) [Ghafir 48-47]. And similar to this in the Quran is much, in which He mentions the statements of the enemies of the messengers and their actions and what they were given of powers of perceptions and movements that did not benefit them when they opposed the messengers. And He, glorified, mentioned what is among those who claim to follow the messengers from the scholars, worshippers, and kings of hypocrisy and misguidance, such as His saying: (O you who have believed, indeed many of the scholars and monks devour the wealth of people unjustly and avert [them] from the way of Allah. And those who hoard gold and silver and spend it not in the way of Allah - give them tidings of a painful punishment) [At-Tawbah 34], and (and they avert from the way of Allah). 'Yasudduna' is used intransitively: it is said 'sadda sududan', meaning he turned away, as He, exalted, said: (And when it is said to them, 'Come to what Allah has revealed and to the Messenger,' you see the hypocrites turning away from you in aversion) [An-Nisa 61]. And it is said: 'sadda ghayrahu yasudduhu' (he turned someone away), and both descriptions combine in them. And like His saying: (Have you not seen those who were given a portion of the Scripture, who believe in jibt and taghut and say about those who disbelieve, 'These are better guided than the believers as to the way'?) [An-Nisa 51]. And in the two Sahihs, from Abu Musa, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: 'The example of the believer who recites the Quran is like that of a citron: its taste is good and its smell is good. The example of the believer who does not recite the Quran is like that of a date: its taste is good but it has no smell. The example of the hypocrite who recites the Quran is like that of a sweet basil: its smell is good but its taste is bitter. The example of the hypocrite who does not recite the Quran is like that of a bitter gourd: its taste is bitter and it has no smell.' So he explained that among those who recite the Quran there are believers and hypocrites.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a prelude to Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the logicians. He first cites Quranic verses and a hadith to establish a key principle: knowledge and intellectual powers do not benefit those who oppose the messengers. He mentions that the Quran abounds with descriptions of the enemies of the messengers, their statements, actions, and the faculties of perception and movement they were given, yet these did not avail them because they opposed the messengers. Then he addresses those who claim to follow the messengers but are hypocrites, citing verses about scholars and monks who devour wealth and turn people away from Allah's path, and about those who were given a portion of the Scripture but believe in false deities and prefer the disbelievers. Finally, he cites a hadith from the two Sahihs about the parable of the believer and the hypocrite regarding Quran recitation, emphasizing that recitation alone does not guarantee sincerity; there are hypocrites among the reciters. This sets the stage for his argument that the logicians' reliance on definitions and syllogisms is insufficient without submission to revelation.

Key Terms
المخالفين للرسل
النفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is the condition of the hypocrite who recites the Quran?
A) His taste is good and his smell is good.
B) His taste is good but his smell is bitter.
C) His smell is good but his taste is bitter.
D) His taste is bitter and his smell is bitter.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge and intellectual powers are only beneficial when accompanied by obedience to the messengers; otherwise, they lead to ruin and hypocrisy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Explain how the hadith of the Quran reciter (sweet basil vs. bitter gourd) illustrates Ibn Taymiyya's point that outward knowledge can coexist with inner hypocrisy.
?
Identify a contemporary argument that claims knowledge alone (e.g., scientific or philosophical reasoning) is sufficient for truth, and refute it using the principle from this lesson that knowledge without obedience to the messengers is futile.

Using the Index of Naqd Mantiq for Targeted Study
Index listing key terms and groups with page references from Naqd Mantiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the index of Naqd Mantiq to locate passages relevant to specific groups or concepts critiqued by Ibn Taymiyya.

Core Idea
An index is a roadmap: it turns a dense critique into a navigable reference.

The pages 384-385 of Naqd Mantiq contain an index listing key terms and groups with page references. While not a logical argument itself, this index is a powerful tool for efficiently locating Ibn Taymiyya's discussions on specific philosophical and theological positions. In this lesson, you will learn how to read and use this index to deepen your understanding of his critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term of interest
Scan the Arabic terms in the index. They are roughly alphabetical. For example, find 'الفلاسفة' (philosophers) or 'المتكلمون' (theologians).
2
Locate the page numbers
Next to each term, a series of numbers indicates pages where the term is discussed. Note that due to OCR, numbers may be misaligned. Verify using logical grouping.
For 'الفلاسفة', see numbers like 24, 302, etc. Cross-check with physical text if possible.
3
Cross-reference with the main text
Turn to those pages in the original Naqd Mantiq to read Ibn Taymiyya's arguments regarding that group. This helps you focus your study.
4
Consider contextual connections
Notice if the same page number appears for multiple terms. This indicates a discussion involving multiple groups, revealing how Ibn Taymiyya weaves his critique.
For example, page 131 appears for several terms, suggesting a passage where multiple groups are compared.
5
Build a research map
Collect page references for related groups (e.g., 'الفلاسفة' and 'المتفلسفة') to see how Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes or conflates them. This helps you map his overall argument structure.
Use the index as a starting point for systematic study.

Commentary
This passage is an index from the back of Naqd Mantiq. It lists key terms, groups, and names with page numbers where they appear in the text. The index is arranged by subject, covering various Islamic sects (e.g., Qadariyya, Karramiyya), schools of thought (e.g., philosophers, theologians), and specific concepts (e.g., 'the syllogists'). The page numbers indicate where these topics are discussed. For a course on logic, such an index is useful for locating discussions of specific logical fallacies or arguments attributed to these groups. Note that the association between some terms and numbers is ambiguous due to OCR issues. The index reflects the breadth of Ibn Taymiyya's critique, ranging from theological groups to philosophical schools.

Key Takeaway
An index is a navigational tool that turns a dense scholarly work into a searchable reference; mastering its use is essential for efficient research.

?
